Make sure your wings are dry before dredging in the flour, should help with them not be so soggy if that's the issue you are having. Also, this recipe is pretty easy to customize to your taste, you can add different sauces and herbs. You can bake these wings on a roasting pan if you want. I've been getting lazy and using parchment paper so that I don't have to use cooking spray, kind of messy, haha. Thanks for everyone's input, I'm so glad you like the recipe!

text:
Excellent! My suggestions to avoid soggy wings (1) Make sure to dry wings before flour dredge, (2) "Rest" wings uncovered in fridge for longer time (3) Line baking sheet or broiler pan with aluminum foil and place cooling rack or equivalent on lined pan, then bake wings on the rack. The grease will drip down into the pan and the wings will cook without soaking in the grease. This is an excellent alternative to fried wings, and being from the Buffalo area, I can say with confidence that these are comparable to those served in this area. Well done!

text:
I have to stop the madness on this board!  This recipe is INCREDIBLE!  Here is what you need to do in order to feel like I do, post-meal:  
Put paper towels down and dry/squeeze your raw wings.  Dredge them in the flour mixture, leave them in the fridge for 45 min-1 hr.  You DO NOT need to leave them in for longer/overnight...I promise. Place them on a cooling rack or a griddle pan (I took my "racks" from my panini press).  Do not dip in the hot sauce mixture and bake wings at 425F for 25 minutes one one side, and then flip for 25 another minutes.  Take them out, dredge them in the sauce mixture (I turned mine twice) and then put them back in the hot oven, under the broiler on low for 5 minutes on each side. If you want to wipe down your pan with paper towels so you're not putting them back into the grease, do it!  I promise they will be amazing!  Re: sauce.  Taste it before you dredge! If you like it hotter, with soy sauce, more garlic and salt, add it! This recipe is great with these additions.  Took longer, but WELL worth it.

Wings were good, but not outstanding.  Based on 200 + reviews, I decided to chill the wings with the flour coating overnight as other reviewers suggested.  Right before baking I dipped in the butter/hot sauce and placed on a wire rack to cook.  Baked these the required 45 minutes and they were, soggy, soggy, soggy with not much flavor.  Pulled them out of the oven and re-dipped in straight hot sauce and then baked an additional 30 minutes with the last 20 minutes at 450 and they FINALLY started crisping.  Once they crisped, they were delicious.  3 stars based on the soggy factor and modification of the recipe to make it "work".  4 stars for taste with the re-dipping!

text:
This recipe offers a good alternative way to make buffalo wings than the traditional deep-fried. It's easy and tastes great. It's good to make ahead for parties. If your wings didn't end up with crispy skin or came out soggy, it may have to do with the wings aren't dry enough. My suggestion is to dry your wings on a drainer after rising. Then pat dry (or even squeeze a little) with paper towel. If your wings are dry enough, they should coat nicely with the flour. Refrigerate without the plastic wrap can also help drying the wings. Do not soak your wings into the butter and hot sauce mixture for too long. If juice comes out during baking, drain it. This should make the crispy skin. I might also try making them in different favors such as lemon pepper or honey lime, etc.

text:
These wings were really quite tasty.  I'm not ready to say that they're the best I've ever had, but they certainly rival that of most restaurants and we were very pleased with them.  I think there are a few musts with these if you want them to be crispy: 1) pat your wings dry before coating with flour and let them sit in the fridge.  Ours sat for an hour and that was perfectly fine.  2) Don't line your pan with foil. While it might make clean-up a little easier, it does nothing to help crisp your wings.  We spread a little olive oil on a cookie sheet and spread them evenly. At about the 30 minute mark we drained any oil or juices off and then put them back in the oven.  3) Don't put the sauce on right away.  We baked ours for about 25 minutes, flipped them, baked for another 15 or so, and THEN rolled them in sauce before putting them back in for another 10 minutes or so. Our wings were crispy and delicious.  Hopes this helps some!

text:
Never, never, never, add flour to chicken wings, baked or fried. For the best tasting and healthier hot wings just cook in oven on cookie tray with non-stick cooking spray for 45 minutes to an hour at 450 degrees. While chicken is baking add your favorite hot wing sauce (and there are many on the market) with as much honey mustard sauce in a bowl and mix real good. When wings are done add to bowl and coat real well. Let cool and eat!

Great recipe for wings. 
Per other reviews, I made sure the wings were very dry before breading, and let sit in fridge for around 3 hours. 
However, when baking, I did half of my wings with dipping in the sauce then baking, the other half I didn't put sauce on until last 10 minutes. Flavor was about the same on both, but the ones that I didn't put the sauce on until the last 10 minutes came out way crispier than wings dipped in sauce before baking.

text:
I currently live in New Zealand but grew up on the East Coast in the US. I have yet to find anywhere here with even passable wings, so I was glad to come across this recipe. I  found some Frank's Redhot at a specialty import store and using that (with a splash of vinegar), they tasted just like home! I followed others advice and baked them on a rack, making sure they were very dry first and brushing on the sauce only after they baked for apx 15 minutes. Then, after baking them for about 15 more minutes, I broiled them until crispy (which does result in a bit of smoke). The first time I made them I refrigerated them before baking for an hour, the second time not at all and I did not see a difference. I served the leftover sauce for dipping along with a homemade bleu cheese dressing and some celery sticks. I cooked them a second time for some of my Kiwi mates and my French bf and they all couldn't get enough!

text:
Wow! My husband and I were really impressed with this recipe-he even said to add it to the regular rotation!  The results were very close to the taste & texture of wings from our favorite wing place.  After reading the reviews, here were the changes I made: 1).  Drying the wings before placing in the flour mixture 2). Placing the wings on a wire rack coated in non-stick spray, then placing the rack over in the baking pan I had refrigerated the wings on.  3).  Cooked the wings at 425 for 45 minutes, turning after 30 minutes 4). I didn't put sauce on the wings before placing in the oven-before turning them over I brushed that side with the sauce, then finished cooking them. After they were done, I placed the wings and sauce in a bag and shook.  Sauce stayed on and coated them well.  They also had a slightly crispy skin.

text:
Incredibly crispy skin and wonderfully moist chicken. 

My husband and I are wing lovers, and we both agree that these are likely the best wings we have ever had. However, you have to follow the adjustments posted by other reviewers to assure that they come out crispy. 

Here are the changes I made for the perfect crispy, delicious wings:
Make sure to pat your wings dry with a paper towel.

Coat in the flour mixture ( I increased the amount of seasoning and added some turmeric and paprika as well).
Place on baking trays and let them sit in the fridge for at least one hour (I let them sit for almost 2 hours).
Preheat oven to 425 or 450 (depending on just how crispy you like your wings)and bake for 25 minutes.
Take them out and flip them over.
Turn heat down to 400 and bake for another 20 minutes.
Remove from oven, let cool slightly, and then dip the fully cooked wings in the sauce. 
Return them to the hot pan and let them sit for a couple of minutes to absorb some of the sauce.
I always have sauce left over, so I pour it into a bowl and use it for dipping.
Watch them closely as you are cooking, so that you can lower the heat if they start to char too much. My husband and I like the skin very crispy and a little charred. 
I served this up with a salad and some fresh garlic green beans. So good! Just made these today for the second time and looking forward to the leftovers.

Tip against soggy wings:
 - dry wings thoroughly with paper towel
 - when baking, place it on a rack so the fat won't 
    soak the wings.
Tip for coating:
 - allow the butter & hot sauce sit until consistency 
    gets thick.  I found out the wings are well 
    coated and retains more of the hot sauce flavor.

text:
This is a great recipe.  You get the fried flavor while baking.  I did a taste test between "Texas Pete's" and  "Crytsal's" hot sauce.  While Texas Pete's had the best smell from the bottle, Crystal's blew it away in every other aspect.  If you look at the texture of the two, Crystal's is way more granular with lots of pepper traces.  Also if you look at Texas Pete's ingredients, there are many perservatives.  Similar to Frank's Red Hot (which may have the best flavor, but has the same additives).  Crystal has the least ingredients, and in my opinion has the best flavor.  Just shake the bottles and look at the texture in your grocery isles.  Hope I saved you some time.  PS dry your wings before flour dredging.

text:
This is a solid recipe! Great alternative to deep frying!  The flour adds a nice crispy texture to the skin and holds the sauce!  As many others mentioned!  Do NOT dip the wings in the sauce before baking them until they are really crispy first!  Pat wings dry, dredge 'em in the flour mixture, let them rest, if you must, then bake them flipping them every 20 mins for about 1 hour or until wings are golden brown and crispy, THEN brush with the butter/hot sauce and bake 10-20 mins longer!  Reality is : all oven temps vary so be mindful of this and adjust temp as needed!   I started at 400, turned down to 350 for 40 mins of the baking so as not to burn the wings but let the fat cook out, then I cranked 'er back up to 400 after I brushed the sauce on!  They were still crispy, not burnt and tasted fab!!!

I personally do not like buffalo wings, but my husband is a big fan. So, I decided that I would give these a try and see if he liked them just as much as the store bought ones. He sure liked these!

I did change a few things based on other peoples reviews. I made sure I patted/squeezed the wings dry with a paper towel before I dredged them. I also baked them on a cooling rack above a baking sheet. One last tweak was that I baked them for 25 minutes on one side, flipped them and cooked them for another 25 minutes *then* I put the sauce on and baked them for an additional 5 minutes. Then I drizzled them with the leftover sauce I made.

Only thing my husband would have liked was for them to be a bit more "saucy". Maybe I'll double dip them next time. Will definitely make these again!

One of the best wings I have ever had. I scaled down the flour to 1/2 cup only because I didn't want to waste the flour. I had a feeling there would be extra and there would of been. Make sure your wings are dried off with a paper towel before you flour them! They set in the fridge for about 3 hours then brushed on the butter/hot sauce mixture. My wings were huge so I cooked mine for about 60 minutes and flipped them three times. Each time I basted the wings with extra Franks Redhot. We like them hot!! These wings turned out perfect! text:
I made these for Super Bowl and they were fantastic!  Definitely bake them on a rack on top of the foil lined baking sheet.  I'm so glad that I did because the juices/sauce will blacken on the bottom and you don't want them cooking in that.  I chose to do 2 flavors, buffalo and terriyaki.  I used 1/4 cup melted butter, 1/4 cup Franks buffalo sauce, and 1/4 cup bbq sauce for the buffalo wings and in another bowl I did 1/4 cup melted butter and 1/2 cup terriyaki sauce.  When the wings were done I felt the terriyaki wings needed more coating so I warmed some terriyaki sauce and recoated them.  The buffalo wings seemed good as is but you could do the same with additional Franks/bbq sauce.  This method produces wings that are easily as tasty as the fried version and the clean up is so easy!  Just throw the foil away.

I read others reviews all the time on here but I have to be honest-this is the first one I have written. I couldn't NOT post a review after making these.  They were outstanding! Husband says better than fried. I did make sure they were perfectly dry. Dried them off with paper towels and let sit in the fridge. I used the seasoned flour(I did add a few extra dashes of this and that) and let them sit in the fridge again for the hour then I baked them as is, flipping them ever 10 minutes or so for about an hour at 375. Made a wing sauce with the butter and Red Hot and some extra spices and when they were done cooking I tossed them in the sauce. They stayed crispy on the outside but were fall apart tender on the inside. I can't wait to make them again-perfect game watching food!

This was fantastic! I used chicken breasts instead (4 large ones), cutting them up into strips.  I coated them, then refrigerated them overnight. text:
While the original recipe is not perfect, it doesn't take a whole lot of alterations to make it absolutely incredible!  I dried my wings well, floured them, and left them in the fridge on a cooling rack for 1.5 hours.  I then proceeded to bake them on the cooling rack on top of an aluminum foil covered tray at 415 for 25 minutes.   Took them out, drained excess juice from the tray, dipped them in sauce, flipped them, and baked another 25 minutes.  
I took them out AGAIN, brushed the tops with sauce, and broiled them on high for 3 minutes on each side, brushing once more after flipping.  The result was crispy, flavorful skin, and tender, juicy meat that slides right off the bone!  What I did obviously took a little more effort, but was well worth it.  I will undoubtably be making these again, thanks!

Alrighty....read all the tips and they turned out not crispy or soggy. 
When I make them again I will: 
1 refrigerate overnight ( 2 hrs not enough )
2 use a rack in the oven ( helped a lot this time)
3 wipe off wings before flour ( great tip !)
4 cook in oven without sauce, dip in ten mins before done. I had to double dip in the sauce this time 
and they weren't coated or spicy enough.
Still a good recipe, will def try again!

1-16-2016 ~Even tho‚Äô I‚Äôve never prepared chicken wings myself, we eat them out often. Hubs‚Äô sensitive innards require that we ask for the sauce on the side  and because of that I know they are tossed in the sauce AFTER they‚Äôre cooked, whether they‚Äôre fried or baked, so I knew that‚Äôs what I‚Äôd be doing when I made these.  But in praise of this recipe I also knew that the flouring would be a good step and would help to achieve a crispy exterior.  Unfortunately, however, they did not brown or crisp sufficiently in the allotted cooking time, so I continued baking them for several more minutes. Frankly, I think what we‚Äôre doing here is to try and achieve the same results with baking as we would with deep frying, and that just won‚Äôt work.  If I try these again, I think I‚Äôll just deal with the extra effort and messiness and fry them.

text:
I thought this recipe was a HIT!!  I refrigerate in the f'lour bag and make sure to shake the wings at a few stages (esp. At the end) to ensure the outer crust is dry and not soggy before baking.  This is also how wings are made in restaurants: fried dry,then tossed in sauce when done cooking.  I cooked them dry (no sauce dip)- once at 400, and the second batch was at 400 then 425 for half the cooking time (because I was cooking something else concurrently), and both times, the wings were crispyand came out very nicely!   It def helps to liberally grease the foil/pan, as the wings can stick when you flip them or when they're done cooking, causing patches of crispy crust to stick and get peeled off from the wings.  I tossed the wings in the sauce after they are done baking, and they were saucy and tasty on the outside, and the skin/flour underneath  was crispy and crunchy, just like fried wings!  I would absolutely recommend this recipe!

text:
Best wings I've ever had!  As one of the reviewers said, I dried the wings well, then dredged in flour/seasoning mixture and refrigerated for at least an hour.  Baked on broiler sheet lined with foil for 25 min per side in 425 deg oven.  I do not like my wings to burn my mouth so I added some BBQ sauce and honey to taste.  Then covered wings with sauce and baked them an additional 5-7 min in broiler until bubbly.  Watch carefully.  Yummy!

text:
I finally found a easy and great wing recipe without all the frying.  I will definately use this recipe from now on.  I doubled this recipe and brined the wings first in salt and brown sugar for a couple hours, then rinsed them.  Then I put Superior soy and chiracha on the wings and let set for a few minutes. I didn't worry about drying the wings before the flour but did give them a shake and poured off any excess moisture in bowl before I put them in the flour.  I did then put them in the fridge for an hour. I didn't sauce first but baked at 425 for 25 min. right on a piece of foil, skin side down first then turned the wings and lowered temp to 400 and basted them with the sauce and cooked for about another 10 to 15 min.  They were very crispy and I have tried all different ways to cook wings and this was by far the best wing recipe I have come across.

This is a fantastic solution to not having the "fried smell" in your home, but still having crispy yummy wings. I did make sure they were patted dry with paper towels before shaking them in the flour Ziploc. I put them in the refrigerator for about 2 hours. I cooked them on a cooling rack over two tinfoil lined cookie sheets. 10 wings a rack, they fit in the oven fine, bottom rack and 2nd to top rack. I cooked them for an hour to ensure maximum crispiness. Though be warned, the drippings made a lot of smoke in the oven and I released the smoke a few times.

text:
Have made this a few times and a few ways. Always wonderful. I like it best when I mix all the spices they suggest and then add onion powder, paprika but skip the salt. I put the spices on the meat directly sometimes and just in the flour other times. Always good either way. I do let the wings sit in the flour for a few hours and make sure the wings are dry when they go into the flour. When I bake them, I do it on a PAM sprayed rack over a cookie sheet.  PAM is VERY important. I don't put the sauce on until they have 10 minutes left or less. Then I pull the wings out and sauce them up. I put them back on the sheet and finish up baking until they are not dripping and the sauce is baked on.  So good.

text:
Excellent! Addictive!  I used 8 chicken legs, any size. Only 1/2 cup flour, 3/4 tsp. cayenne pepper, 3/4 tsp. garlic powder, 1/2 tsp salt. I used chicken shears to cut off skin for lower cholesterol, which actually helped the spices to be more on the meat.
Shook one leg at a time in bag for better coverage.
Placed a tiny spot of olive oil on foil where leg was placed.  Refrigerated 1 1/2 hrs.  
Put some Frank's hot pepper sauce in small bowl, Added 2-3 T. of olive oil. Mixed and dipped one leg at a time in bowl, put a spot of olive oil on foil. Put on leg.  Baked about 40-45 mins. Did not turn. Incredible!  Could have eaten 4-6..Husband loved them. Great for leftover warm-up or snacks.  Grandsons would have devoured them if they had been here. Very cheap to make, quick and easy.

text:
I read at least 50 of the reviews before making my second time.  First time out I followed the recipe and they were very soggy.  After these tweaks to the recipe my second batch of wings were excellent.  My advaice is to be sure to dry the wings well after cleaning,  use the parchment paper and not foil, leave them in the oven for 2 hours not just one, turn the wings twice once they have started to brown, do not dip in sauce until AFTER you bake them (ensures them to be cripy and not soggy).  I also used Franks Red Hot Wings - Buffalo sauce instead of the regular flavor.  Great if you like less heat in your wings and serving to kids.

My to-to recipe for wings.  I'm convinced the method is the key to success.  Be sure the wings are dry before dredging and then dry them again in the fridge after dredging.  I usually bake for 20 minutes per side and then do a setting on my oven - convection roast - for 5-10 minutes per side.  The convection roast really browns them up and crisps them.  I only put the hot sauce on half on account of my finicky kids but the plain ones are also very tasty.

text:
So, I originally started making the 'Boneless Buffalo Wings' from this website. After I mixed the flour & ingredients from that recipe, I began to read the reviews for this one & decided to go this route. Pretty much the only difference is paprika & amounts of other spices added (which everyone does anyways). I read the first few pages of reviews & did this - other than change the flour recipe, I blotted/squeezed extra water out of the chicken before I floured it, let it sit in the fridge for more than an hour, I used the cooling rack in the oven, but forgot to spray it, so the wings stuck a little bit, I didn't put the sauce on (I used that Frank's stuff, they wouldn't have been as good with another brand) until they were done cooking & cooled (I used butter Pam & sprayed the wings before I put them in the oven). I didn't flip them either. After I let them cool, I sauced them, then on a couple I added cajun seasoning on top of the hot sauce/butter mix. Mine were super crispy and perfect, so if yours weren't, try what I did & you'll love it! Also, after I battered the wings, I made ranch with the Hidden Valley Ranch dip mix and light sour cream (I don't think the fat-free sour cream works/tastes well for ranch) so it would have time for the flavors to mix. I plan on flouring wings the night before the weekend (when I really crave them).

text:
Delicious! After trying these, my son refuses to go back to the frozen Buffalo wings I used to buy! They're a lot of work, but worth it. I made a few changes. Do not use foil, the wings stick to it horribly! Instead, I used parchment paper. First of all, I added 1 tsp of cayenne pepper, 1 tsp of garlic powder, and 1/2 tsp of salt to the flour. (Because my guys love hot food)  I followed other reviewers's suggestions and thoroughly dried the wings before dredging them in the flour. Also to the sauce, I added a dash of black pepper, a dash of hot pepper flakes,  and a dash of garlic powder. Also, I used only 1/3 c. of butter and 1/2 c. of hot sauce because the sauce is not hot enough. Next, do not dip in the hot sauce mixture.  Bake wings at 425F for 25 minutes one one side, and then flip for 25 another minutes. Take them out, dredge them in the sauce mixture and then put them back in the oven, under the broiler on low for 5 minutes on each side.  Amazing! Going to make a ton for the Super Bowl.

text:
I have made them this way for years, and they are great.  

I found I can CUT a lot of calories by this method.  I skip the flour, butter, and dipping in hot sauce.   I bake them on a cookie sheet lined with foil, at 425 degrees for about 1 hour until they are golden and crispy.   This renders out most of the fat under the skin.    I don't use butter in my sauce anymore either.   I roll them through the hot sauce, straight from the bottle,  and enjoy them with a great lite Blue Cheese dressing.

text:
This is a very tasty and easy alternative for those that would rather bake their wings than fry them. You will have to play with the cayenne and hot sauce portions to get your desired spicy taste. Using the portions listed will give you a mild spicy taste, in my opinion. To improve the crispy turnout after baking, I would suggest: 1) make sure the wings are thoroughly thawed; 2) pat dry the wings (using paper towels) before placing them in the flour mixture; 3) after flouring, place them in the refrigerator for an hour (the overnight suggestions I‚Äôve been reading seem to be overkill); 4) bake the wings BEFORE rolling them in the sauce (25 mins on one side, 15 on the other); 5) drain the oil from the pan then roll the wings in the sauce, place them back on the pan; 6) cook for another 10 mins or so‚Ä¶.until the wings get nice and crispy. If you prefer wet wings, I‚Äôd suggest making extra sauce to toss the wings in afterwards.

text:
I felt the need to offset some of the 1 star "I didn't follow directions and it didn't turn out, so I don't like it" reviews. 

If you follow it, it will work.  I used fresh wings; maybe people are getting soggy ones if they use frozen wings?

It's important to NOT crowd your pan (you do not want them touching), and make sure to use enough non-stick spray so you get all of the crispy goodness left on your wing.

The only modification I do is heat up some extra sauce (no butter this time, just sauce out of the bottle) and toss the crispy cooked wings in it at the very end, just to get that little extra zing.  Basically I originally did this because I had extra sauce, but not enough to keep for something else.

This was my 1st time making buffalo wings (for NYE party)....and they were AMAZING!!!  I am not the least interested in trying a fried recipe!  I tweaked a couple of things for my liking.   I basically added more garlic powder, cayenne pepper and Lawry's season salt than suggested. In addition I added a little black pepper, paprika and onion powder.  Something else I did different was Once the chicken was completely finished and crisp, I placed all the chicken in a large skillet with the already prepared Franks hot sauce and butter sauce.  This was the first and only time the chicken was mixed with the sauce.  So the chicken was crispy yet full of sauce and juicy on the inside.  Served with blue cheese for dipping.  It was the best this way!!!!!!!!

text:
I hate to be one of those people that changes somebody else's recipe around and then reviews but I am admittedly,a very picky cook and Buffalo Wings have been a favorite of mine since childhood so it is only natural for me to try,try and try again until it comes out perfect.I mean,literally,these Buffalo Wings are perfect and a favorite of my family.
If you want authentic Buffalo Wings I strongly recommend that you follow Chef John's Buffalo Wing Sauce recipe right here on Allrecipes.com BUT follow the first part of this recipe where you coat and bake the wings.
The combination of the two great recipes will produce delicious,authentic tasting Buffalo Wings right  in your own kitchen.
I lay down several sheets of paper towels and layer the wings, batch at a time on top and then press down on the wings with more paper towels to get them as dry as possible before coating in the flower mix.
I also prep them several hours(4-6) before baking time so that they can rest in the fridge a bit.
Make sure you are generous when spraying your foil lined sheet pan(s) with cooking spray as they have a tendency to stick if you don't.
Turning them after 24 minutes is very important so make sure that you set your timer.
They are crispy every time.

text:
These are great!  We've made them twice now, and both times have been successful!  We use frozen "party wings" (they're a little bigger/meatier than the others).  I defrost them in water, which doesn't take long, and then put pat them off & start the recipe off w/ the flour mixture.  We usually use extra garlic in our flour mix (we use extra garlic in EVERYTHING!), and sometimes a little extra cayenne to kick up the heat, and ball park it on the salt (I hate measuring; hence, my complete inability to bake!)  I do let these rest on an elevated grated surface (think a cookie cooling rack), above a foil-lined cookie sheet, for at least an hour, in the fridge.  I dunk them very quickly (enough to coat) in the butter/red hot mix, and then bake immediately (on the same elevated rack - to allow the heat to circulate better).  I have found that the red hot mix isn't really enough to coat 20 large wings, so we usually end up having to make extra.  It would probably work with smaller wings though.  I turn them about 1/2 way through cooking.  In the last few minutes, I put the rack under the broiler on high to really crisp up the edges & brown them a little - just for a couple of minutes. They DO take about 45 minutes to an hour to cook, depending on size.  Also, I've found that the "flat" wings tend to cook a little better (melt in your mouth vs. work at it) than the drummies, even though I personally prefer drummies regularly.  This recipe is great - just plan on a couple of hours!

I was looking for a healthier alternative to delivered (deep-fried) buffalo wings, and this recipe came very close to being 5 stars, however, it left me wishing for a slightly stronger flavor.  Next time I will try adding more cayenne pepper and possibly garlic powder.  I followed the advice of many, many reviews that said you should dry the wings before putting them in the bag with the dry seasoning mix, so that it sticks better to the wings.  I measured the butter and placed it in a glass bowl and put it in the microwave for 30-45 seconds in order to melt it.  Because the recipe says it's for 20 wings and I had a little bit more than that I was concerned it wouldn't yield enough for all the wings, so I decided to double the recipe.  I had a lot of flour and butter/hot sauce mix left over, so next time I am going to make the wings without doubling the recipe to see if that is enough, I'm sure it will be.  Don't forget the blue cheese dip on the side!

text:
This recipe was great. I altered it by - using chilli powder instead of cayenne, dried wings thoroughly using paper towels, baked on a rack as most people advised, did not turn, baked for 35 minutes, removed to immerse each wing entirely in the sauce then returned to oven for another 15 minutes.

I make  a VERY hot wing sauce of 1/2 cup butter, 1/4 cup sriracha, 1/4 cup habanero pepper sauce, a mild hot wing sauce using 1/2 cup butter & 1/2 cup sriracha and a sweet sauce using 1/2 cup butter 1/2 cup honey.

Thank you to the original poster, and the AR community for giving such great feedback. These delicious wings really made our Super Bowl party and my older relatives were amazed, asking "how after 40 years of cooking can such a young man make such delicious wings for us?!!?"

text:
Made these for a football game gathering, and they were a big hit. I was very concerned about the baked wings being crispy enough, and these were, with some adjustments.  Baked at 425 for 45 minutes, poured the juices off the pan, turned the wings, and cooked for another 45 minutes.  Then I tossed the wings in Frank's Red Hot and returned to the oven for another 10 minutes.  No need to use the butter - wings are fattening enough.  I used lots of Pam, but did have trouble with the wings sticking to the foil.  I'll probably use more vegetable oil next time.  I was intimidated, but these were really pretty easy.  Now that I know how, I'll make these again sometime.

text:
Thanks Leesah for this GREAT recipe!
These wings are awesome! My family dislikes wings swimming in Buffalo wing sauce because of the mess. This recipe has the full Buffalo sauce flavor w/o the mess. Everyone raved about the wings!
Great bar style food w/o the expensive bar prices!
IMPORTANT ‚Äì crack all of the wing joints first.
I always rinse and thoroughly pat dry any meat before dredging them in flour and I refrigerate them for at least an hour before cooking them, I do the same with any meat that has an egg wash. Doing so ensures that the breading won‚Äôt get soggy and will remain on the meat during the cooking process. I refrigerated the wings for 90 minutes after dredging them in the flour mix.
I followed the rest of the recipe instructions and baked them with the wing tips (yes, I like the crispy skin on wing tips) facing up at 400¬∞F for 30 minutes, flipped the wings and baked for another 30 minutes till they were nicely browned and crispy. I served the wings with Bleu Cheese salad dressing, celery sticks and carrot sticks.
I served the choice of beer or iced tea as beverages to accompany this dish.
Yummo!!!

text:
This is a solid recipe for oven baked buffalo wings. I make two changes in procedure to help prevent soggy wings. I bake them on a rack to let the grease drip down, and I bake them without the butter and sauce. Once they're cooked, I melt the butter in a frying pan and stir in the sauce. I then drop the wings into the hot frying pan and toss to coat.

This were REALLY good, particularly for my first time making wings. I took the advice of the reviewers and baked these on wire racks. My family says these were the best wings they've every had...counting "professional" ones from BW's.  They were tender and crispy and very flavorful. I didn't use the 5 t of cayenne, just probably 1 t, and some garlic and onion powders and salt.  I did add about 1/2 cup of Panko bread crumbs. I used an actual cookie sheet and would recommend using something closer to a jelly roll pan (something with some sides) as they cook out some and the cookie sheet was in danger leaking drippings onto the bottom of the oven. They were a little labor intensive but well worth it. Thanks for the recipe!

These are amazing Buffalo wings, baked not fried. I followed others suggestions and blotted the wings well before flouring them. I cooked them on a cookie cooling rack over a jelly roll pan. Spray the rack well with cooking spray so the wings don't stick. I flipped them half way through the cooking time. We like our wings spicy, so I used just a quarter cup of butter. Next time I may use less. I shook the baked wings in the hot sauce/butter mix. They were delicious, not greasy at all, and are now a Sunday staple!

text:
I will never fry buffalo wings again after realizing I can make such crispy delicious wings in the oven. I made some changes to the recipe though. I omitted the garlic powder and added paprika. To prevent wasting spices and for more flavor I seasoned the chicken directly, and then added to the bag of plain flour. I kept them in the bag instead of transfering them to a baking sheet. They absorbed more of the coating this way. Make sure you keep the wings in the flour for at least an hour though, its a must. I also didn't add the sauce until after baking, and I don't think the wings would've came out as crispy, or crispy at all if i did. I used a much higher ratio of hot sauce to butter because I love the heat.

text:
This is our go to baked buffalo chix wing recipe. To keep the wings crispy, we bake the wings without the sauce. After baking, we then toss them in the sauce. It also helps to cook the wings on top of a wire cooling rack so they sit above the baking sheet and don't get soggy in all the juices. You also don't have to turn them half way when doing it this way. We also like a spicier sauce so do 1/4 cup butter to 3/4 cup Frank's hot sauce, perfect!!

text:
Wings do not need any butter. The problem with mixing the sauce with the butter is that you don't get that much sauce on the wings. I like my wings crispy and spicy. Next time I'll add more cayenne pepper to the flour (twice the recipe), no salt (because the buffalo sauce is seasoned enough), and no butter (because the skin has enough fat). I cooked them on 425 F for 20 minutes each side, then BROILED each side for 5 minutes to get the skin toasted. I recommend getting ready to cook wings (frozen perhaps) so you don't have to go through the trouble of cutting the pieces (not good butcher skills here).

First time ever making Buffalo wings.  As soon as I started, I realized I made a big mistake - I didn't thaw the wings beforehand, so I had to do it in the microwave.

In the end, I followed most of comments and dried the (more or less thawed) wings with a paper towel.  I am a hot head, but didn't think I needed the cayenne pepper.  I figured that 1/2 cup of Franks hot sauce was enough, and it was.  Heat wise, it was about the same as a typical "hot" chicken wing at a restaurant.  Perfectly balanced.

Like the other reviewers, I dipped them in sauce towards the end of the bake.

The main problem with these is that I didn't make enough.  My family cleaned them out.  My wife claims that they were better than her fried chicken, something that is physically impossible :)

text:
I made them according to recipe, using parchment paper rather than foil, and I had extra wings, so I made a batch per recipe and the method of not dipping them in the butter mixture before baking. The original recipe way was far better!! I did however, drain the fat from the first batch before turning. They browned up very nicely, and were very crispy,  and the spice was perfect. I will definitely make them again, as per recipe!

***********EDIT TO ADD ANOTHER VERSION - Last night I roasted a whole chicken using this recipe using the same steps - DRY the chicken, dredge in the flour mixture, refrigerate for 2hrs, preheat oven to 375 on convection, pour the butter sauce over the chicken and brush onto spots that got missed, put 1/2 lemon inside the bird, baked approx 1-1/2 hrs (use your own judgement as oven temps vary). I put the chicken on a rack in a roasting pan and added some water to prevent burning the pan.
This chicken was awesome! Nice crispy skin and full of flavour - adjust spices to your personal liking. I added more heat. This is going to be my go to for wings and roasted whole chicken!

text:
I live in Buffalo NY, the birthplace of "Buffalo Wings" and these were just as good as anything here, without the frying. Hometown wings never ever use flour, but if you want to bake, the flour adds a level of crispness you wouldn't have otherwise. Delicious, crisp and so good. The only suggestion I would have is to wait to the end to dip in the butter/hot sauce. Dip hot wings into sauce using a set of tongs and just set back on the cookie sheet in the oven for a few more minutes. They'll be crispy and saucy. Enjoy this great recipe.

text:
I have made this recipe five times and each time it gets better.  I changed some of the methodology per the advice of other reviewers: 1) I made sure the wings were very dry. 2) I didn't have a baking rack and instead used a roasting pan (wings came out nice and crispy!) 3)I did not refrigerate after dredging. 4) I used the modified amount of cayenne pepper (1/2 tsp). 5) I baked them without the sauce half way through on 400 then brushed on liberal amounts of wing sauce mixture and baked them for the rest of the time on 450. 6) after taking them out brushed on some more sauce to have a crispy yet saucy texture.  This review has been Hubby tested and approved of the improved methodology :)

text:
This recipe was amazing.  I ended up letting the wings sit in the flour mixture overnight (more from laziness and time constraint).  Since they were slightly damp, some of the flour had become pasty but I just added more flour and they coated fine.  I followed the advice of another reviewer (Vandygirl29) and baked for 25 min on each side at 425 on a cooling rack.  They came out amazingly crispy.  I then actually used Sweet Baby Rays buffalo wing sauce to bake for an additional 5 min and then coated them in sauce to my liking once done cooking.  These were absolutely amazing.  I'll probably be making my own buffalo wings from now on.  This recipe can also easily be used for other flavors.  I'm a fan of Wing Stop's lemon pepper flavor.  Can't wait to do that next!

Fantastic!  I made these wings last night for the Super Bowl.  I made primarily as the recipe stated except I added a little more seasoning to the flour mixture.  Then...as another reviewer suggested I baked on a rack in a foil lined cookie sheet at 425 for 20 minutes, flipped the wings and baked for another 20 minutes.  Coated with sauce and broiled for 3 minutes, turned and broiled for 3 minutes more.  After broiling I coated in sauce again.  They came out moist inside, crispy outside and had tons of fantastic flavor.  They were devoured by all and made for easy cleanup on a busy day!

None
text:
My husband loves these! Excellent flavor & the coating step is key. We use Frank RedHot or Texas Pete. 
After making these several times, I have a couple slight modifications that really work. Do not refrigerate more than 2 hours. I know many recommend refrigerating overnight, I humbly disagree. I tried that. I had washed/patted dry the wings but the coating still absorbed chicken juices after resting 8+ hours. When baked, the coating texture turned puffy; not crispy. 
When making the sauce, reserve 1/4 of it. Bake as instructed. When turning the wings over, brush the remaining sauce on. Finally, non-stick foil made them crisp the best so far. You can do parchment but they will not have the "crisp" factor..but they're still good!

I'm kind of a traditional wings snob, so I tried this mostly out of curiosity, just to see how they'd work out. Like a previous reviewer, I found 400 degrees to be too low; the wings didn't start to brown or crisp until I increased the heat to 450. I also had to re-dip the wings again after cooking, which decreased what little crispiness they had. Fun to try, and I'd probably make them again, but I wouldn't serve them to a fellow wing-lover, if that makes sense. (Note: Used Chef John's Buffalo sauce recipe from this site. THE BEST.)

This was a great recipe.  Based on several others, I did make a few changes to the cooking process--but not the ingredients.  I "dried" the wings for about 10 minutes between layered sheets of paper towel.  I put all the wings in the flour mixture, tossed, and left them right in the bag while they sat in the fridge for an hour. They were absolutely delicious and will be a staple for future parties!

text:
Just made these and they came out very crispy. The important thing is to place them on a cookie rack in your baking sheet, not on the sheet itself. That way they won't be sitting in their own drippings and it makes them easier to remove without tearing the meat off the wings since there is less surface area for them to stick to. As others suggested I sauced them at the very end. This is probably the closest you're going to get to a crispy fried wing without actually frying it. I could taste the flour a little bit, but the sauce pretty much masks it.

text:
Excellent flavor! Nice texture. YUM! To make this recipe even healthier (which is why I was looking for a baked wings recipe) I used whole wheat flour and cut up boneless/skinless chicken breasts and boneless/skinless thighs into fourths to make "wing" size pieces. As others have mentioned, the secret to crispy wings is definitely DRY wings and plenty of fridge time. I also made a dipping sauce with 16oz. plain low fat yogurt, mix in 1 mashed avocado and a pack of low sodium ranch spices. While nothing can truly replace the greasy goodness of chicken skin and oil, this is definitely close enough to satisfy a wing craving without blowing your diet!

text:
I consider myself somewhat of a novice in the kitchen, but I love to dabble and try new things that DON'T require deep-frying.  In looking for a fun and simple baked wings recipe, I stumbled across this gem.  As you can see, the ingredients do not require any special trips to the grocery store (all of the ingredients I consider to be cooking essentials).  Additionally, I did not have any problems whatsoever with the moisture of the finished product.  In fact, what I absolutely wanted to avoid were super-dry, crispy wings.  I was very satisfied with the taste and texture of this recipe, and just for fun, I used a few different varieties of sauces as coatings.  (I recommend Frank's Red Hot Sweet Heat BBQ.)  The only tip I would offer to the next person who attempts this recipe is to use a non-stick baking sheet if at all possible... just reduces the cleanup effort.  Thanks for posting, Leesah.

text:
This is a good recipe. I tried it out tonight and everyone loved it. I didn't have the cayenne and garlic powder so I used a little sage and paprika instead. I did half a batch with hot sauce and the other half plain for the kids. I floured the wings in the bag and baked it in a 400 deg oven, I didnt brush the meat with oil as the meat had enough fat to sweat out whilst baking and this gave the flour coating a crispier finish. Brushed on the hot sauce for half the batch once the wings were done and sent them back in the oven for 5-10 mins to finish. My mother in law loved it. Btw I had some chicken leg meat cut into large chunks and cooked with the wings in the same way and my daughter said they tasted like chicken nuggets, but better. All round a good recipe.

text:
I have made this several times and it is always a hit. The first few times I made it just as it is described and they were wonderful. However, I decided to take the advice of a few other reviewers this last time I made it and it made a huge difference. Definitely pat the chicken dry before dredging it in flour to help the sogginess as well as baking it on a cooling rack (or something similar) with a drip tray underneath. Also, I baked the chicken for 30 minutes without the sauce and then dipped it in the sauce for the last 15 minutes and they came out crispy and perfect. This is definitely the way to go. I also like to prepare the chicken the night before and let it sit in the fridge overnight. Anything you can do make the skin crispier the better they will turn out. If you do all these things your wings come out very crispy to the point that you almost can't tell that they weren't deep fried. This is a great recipe, I make it almost every week during football season.

text:
When company was coming I looked for an alternative to frying batch after batch of wings. These were pretty good but I still prefer the fried ones. How I made mine: I baked them on a non-stick rack for an hour without any sauce. I then dipped them and returned to the over for 5 minutes. I didnt have any garlic powder so I simmered some fresh in the butter before adding the hot sauce. These werent spicy enough for us and I had already changed the hot pepper sauce ratio to 3/4 cup pepper sauce to 1/4 cup butter. Next time I will increase the cayenne to 1 1/2 tsp. I had no problem with sogginess, I made sure my wings were really dry and left them in the fridge for way longer than an hour. Make sure to turn them when half done to crisp both sides.

This was a very good recipe for buffalo wings. I did make some modifications to the recipe however. I used the small party wing instead of the regular size wings. I only put the wings in the fridge for about 30 minutes. I also increased the amount of garlic powder to 1 tablespoon. I baked the wings on 425 for 1 hours. Me and my boyfriend ate all 20 wings, they were just that good.

text:
So good!  I followed the bit of advice and cooked them halfway before dipping them in the sauce.  I also broiled them for a minute at the end.   A tip that works for baking or frying wings...let them cool and dry out for about 5 minutes before adding the sauce at the end.  It crisps them up even more.  Warm up the sauce and don't add it until right before you eat them.

text:
I read the reviews before I tried this recipe so I didn't make the mistake of adding 5 teaspoons of cayenne.  I followed the recipe almost to the letter with a couple of exceptions.  I used a family sized package of 25 drumettes and coated them in the flour mixture the day before.  They were in the fridge, uncovered, for about 18 hours.  I baked them in two batches.  The first batch I coated in the oil/hot sauce mixture before baking (20 minutes on one side, 25 on the other).  The second batch I baked for 20 minutes, removed from the oven, basted with the sauce, turned them over, basted that side and baked for another 25 minutes.  Both batches were really crispy and delicious.  My husband, who doesn't much care for hot wings, loved them.

text:
I was really hoping these would turn out crunchy since I like the crunchy kind best so I did as some of the reviewers suggested and baked the wings before I coated them in the sauce.  I did not leave them in the fridge first since I figured that was a moot point so maybe that was a mistake.  The wings were not crunchy but I'm also thinking I might could have tried cooking them longer?  I will probably play around with this recipe some more.  If you like spicy you will probably want to use less butter/more hot sauce.  I had doubled the recipe (we were feeding lots of people) but the sauce I only did 3/4 cup of butter and 1 cup of Frank's hot sauce and there was MORE than enough sauce.  I saved the extra sauce and put it in the fridge for topping burgers and such.

text:
There was more than enough of the flour mixture in the bag so I made a few extra. It made about 30 wings total, which is half of the "party pack" from Costco. I placed them in 2 foil-line baking sheets and baked them in the oven before adding any of the sauce (they won't get soggy).  Flip after 25 minutes. Take out after 20 more. To make the sauce I just mixed a stick of butter and the whole bottle of Frank's Red Hot (Xtra Hot) in a glass baking dish. Place wings in glass dish & turn to coat both sides. Put dish in oven 5 minutes. My husband says they're really good.

text:
Sunday before the Super Bowl I was digging around in the freezer for something to eat while watching the game. I found a few things that needed to be tossed and a few things that the wife and I could snack on. And I ran across a package of chicken wings. I put then in water to defrost and came here to Recipes.com to see what I had saved in the way of chicken wing recipes. This is the one I chose because I had all the ingredients.

After the wings defrosted I found I only had four whole wings which separate into only 8 drumletts and blades so I halved the recipe. Also, I'm off gluten so I used a gluten-free flour (Better Batter) which works really well in most cases but tends to brown more quickly than wheat flour. This tendency to brown is actually an advantage in this case. I followed the recipe as given with the amounts halved (Note 3/4 cup = 12 Tablespoons which means I used 6 Tablespoons of flour).

Chicken wings are fatty and baking them produces lots of grease. Next time I make them I will put them on a rack. Turning them in all that grease was not something I wanted to do so I blotted the grease with paper towels during the turn-them-over process.

The flavor was very nice - a bit mild for my taste and I'll up the heat next time, the texture was excellent - crispy on the outside and juicy on the inside, the 45 minute cooking time was just right. Even my wife, who is not generally a wings person gave them two thumbs up. This has become my go-to wings recipe.

text:
This is such a crowd-pleaser! Everyone loves these chicken wings! This is the kind of recipe that you are so happy to have found. This recipe definitely added joy to the life of some people around me (including myself)! Thank you so much for sharing the recipe!!

Since I make this so often nowadays, I have perfected the easier quicker way of making this. I make a big batch of the flour in advance. We like garlic and the heat, so I used to triple the amount of galic powder and cayenne, but I am now back to doubling them to fit to everyone's taste. If you use microwave to melt the butter, the sauce will be too runny and will not stick to the chicken very well. I usually microwave the butter and mix it with hot sauce in advance, so it is the right consistency when I dredge chicken in it. In fact, recently, I have developped new method of placing several chicken pieces on a plate and pour 1 -2 table spoonful of sauce on top of it. Then, spread the sauce to coat the chicken pieces evenly gently rubbing them against each other before placing them back on the foild pan. Chilling the chicken definitely helps the coating to be more firm, yield crispier Buffalo wings. You can flour large amount of chicken wings at once, put them in smaller bags 10-20 pieces of party wings in each bag, thaw them in the fridge a day before coating them in hot sauce and baking. This way, the wings are already perfectly chilled. What a great recipe. (Ugh... one more confession... I actually even have the h

text:
Excellent Wings without the fat of frying!  I've made baked wings before, but all I did was throw the wings in a dish and cover with Franks Buffalo Wing sauce.  These are MUCH better.  Be sure to completely dry out your wings.  And don't use those that are big bags of frozen wings with "extra liquid added."  Get fresh wings/drummettes and squeeze them completely dry with paper towels.  Be sure to place them uncovered on the prepared baking sheet (just as the recipe says).  When finished, if you still want them crispier, just put them under the broiler for 5-10 minutes.  These are DELICIOUS!  THANK YOU for the recipe---it's a keeper.

text:
I made this without making any changes to the recipe. It is an easy recipe but the next time I'll make a few changes to avoid the trouble I got into. 1) double the dipping sauce (I used Presidents Choice Buffalo wings sauce), lightly whipping the sauce and melted butter together thickens it. 2) add about a half tsp of paprika to the sauce (I like a more vibrant "red" to the dish if using the PC sauce again. 3) definitely use a grill insert over a roasting pan, Do not use a cookie sheet!  grease from the wings dripped over the sides and smoke poured out of the oven setting off the smoke alarms. 4) don't pack the wings tightly together to get it all in one pan, give a little space for the wings to cook evenly. The flavour of the wings was just right -- not too spicy. I will make this recipe again but will definitely avoid the mistakes I made with the type of pan I used to bake the wings in. I think the grill insert will make the wings nice and crispy.

THese wings deserve  more stars than I am allowed. Seasoned perfectly, so easy to do, and crispy too! For those who had a problem with soggy chicken wings, I have the solution. Your wings should be partially frozen when you cut them up. Then when you add the flour mix, there is no wetness at all. I also place  one of my cookie-cooling racks on the baking sheet. This gives an even, crispy crust and you don‚Äôt have to turn them over half-way through baking.  Be sure to spray the rack before use.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Have been looking for a really good, and easy, wing recipe to make at home because I've noticed restaurant wings are getting quite expensive. This recipe does NOT disappoint! 

I followed the recipe ingredients to a T, but followed another reviewer's advice when cooking them. I made sure the wings were dry before I dredged them in flour. Then I sprayed a cookie sheet with olive oil spray, placed the wings on it and put them in the fridge for an hour. Baked them for 25 minutes and when I took them out to turn them, a few were stuck to the sheet, so I placed the wings in a bowl and poured a little EVOO on the cookie sheet and spread it around. Put the wings back on and baked the other sides for 15 min. Removed them from the oven and dredged them in the Buffalo sauce and cooked them another 10 minutes. They came out crispy on the outside, but still nice and moist on the inside. I really believe using the EVOO on the cookie sheet, instead of using the spray, is what makes them crispy. 

My husband and son said there wasn't nearly enough sauce on the wings when they tried them(they like ALOT of sauce), so I put them back in the bowl and tossed them with Frank's Red Hot buffalo sauce. When they were finished, they both went on and on about how good they were and asked to make this a permanent recipe in our house.

text:
These were very good but I made some changes based on other reviews. I thoroughly dried the chicken with paper towels before dredging in flour then I put them on trays, uncovered, in the fridge for 1 hour. I did not put sauce on them until almost the end of cooking. I baked them on a jelly roll pan cover with foil at 425 for 25 minutes then I drained the pan, turned the wings and baked 25 more minutes. The wings were super crispy. I then dipped the wings in the sauce & put under the broiler for about 3 minutes. These were not soggy at all. I will definitely make again. One of the things I have learned over the years is that a low sided pan (like a jellyroll pan) allows for better crisping than a regular baking pan when making wings or ribs. It is also important to pour off any fat from the pan at the half way cooking point.

text:
Being the first time I make wings, this recipe was a good way to start: very simple and not much preparation.  What takes the most time is refrigerating them and baking them (not much work at all). 
I read another rating of this recipe and there was a problem with soggyness, but I did not encounter that. What I did to ensure I did not have this problem was bake them for 20 min at 400F, then turn them and bake them at 425F, and once they were fully cooked, I turned on the broiler for 525F. They came out crispy and well cooked. 
I will be using this recipe again.
4 stars only because though they were good, they were not amaaazing.

text:
These were excellent. Thank goodness for the extensive reviews, I always read many of them before attempting recipes on here. I took what I thought were some of the best tips to avoid sogginess and swimming in grease. I took care to trim and then seriously dried each wing before dredging. The pan was in the fridge for about 5 hours. I put the wings on racks that fit the pan to keep them from sitting in their own grease and covered the bottom with foil for easy cleanup. I cooked at 400 F for 25 min without the sauce, flipped them and cooked for 15 min more, and finally took them out and rolled each in the buffalo sauce, drizzling more on top, and then cooked for a final 10 minutes. They were crispy, spicy, juicy, simply wonderful. I made extra buffalo sauce for dipping and it was a perfect complement to the homemade ranch dressing I also used for dipping. Will definitely will make again. Oh one final thing- I like spice, I used two tsp of cayenne and a full teaspoon of the other seasonings in the flour blend.

These were a huge hit.  A little time consuming, with prepping but so worth it.  You definitely have to make sure the chicken is as dry as possible before flouring.   Flour sticks better.   I refrigerated mine for over an hour, but only because I was in the middle of a project, not sure if this time matters.  Then, what I did, on aluminum foil, 20 minutes, flipped for another 20.  I removed chicken from pan, there was quite a bit of juices. I threw that out. As far as the seasoned flour, I followed directions, the taste was fine for us.

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
I've noticed many people saying their wings were soggy. There are a couple reasons this can happen. The first is make sure when you buy your chicken wings they haven't been soaked in a brine. To know if they have, check the ingredients list. If salt is on it,  it's been brined. The chicken sweats the brine liquid while cooking which leaves you with soggy wings. The other is not making sure the wings are very dry before coating with the flour and not re-flouring just before adding to the baking sheet. The second round of lightly flouring is imperative to get a crispy baked wing. 
I made half a batch according to the recipe, the other half using what I know.  The recipe batch were soggy. My double floured batch were crispy. That aside this recipe is fantastic. The flavor is perfection.

text:
No grease, no mess and taste just as good as deep fried wings.  Everyone I serve them to loves them and asks for the recipe.  I do a couple things different though.   After refrigerating, I place the dredged wings on a wrack place on top of the pan so the hot oven air circulates all around the wings.   I DO NOT put the wing sauce on them until after they cook about an hour, turning half way through the time.   I take them out of the oven and place them in a lidded bowl with the sauce and shake to coat well.  I then put them back in the oven for another 15 minutes.  This insures crispy wings.

My family loved these wings! We followed the directions except that we baked the wings at 450 degrees for 30 minutes, turning over after 20 minutes. One big difference is that we added the sauce AFTER baking. That way, we were all able to add as much sauce as we liked. My husband drenched his wings and I lightly sprinkled my wings with sauce. We used Frank's Wing Sauce(no added butter). My son used a less spicy BBQ sauce on his wings. We will definitely use this recipe again.

text:
Easy and very tasty recipe but I did make a few minor alterations... From reading the other reviews I was sure to dry them well with paper towels before coating with the flour mixture, instead of placing the wings directly in the pan I put them on a wire rack so the juices would drain into the pan and my chicken wouldn't be soggy, and lastly, after dipping the wings into the butter/hot sauce mixture,  I baked the wings for 25 minutes turned them over and baked an additional 35 mins.  They were crisp and flavorful.

text:
I dredged the chicken wings in the flour mixture before reading the reviews, so I forgot to dry the wings before dredging. I let them sit an hour, and then put them into a 450 oven without dipping them into the hot sauce mixture (I increased the temperature because I was afraid they would be soggy). I cooked them 15 on each side, then took them out to dip in the hot sauce mixture. I lowered the temp to 425, then put them back in for another 20 minutes. They came out very crispy and delicious. 
I used one baking sheet line with foil and one glass Pyrex baking dish. The wings came out the same, so I guess you can use either one (but the baking sheet was a lot easier to clean--just  throw away the foil).

text:
Made these for Superbowl yesterday, but took advice on paper towel squeezing/pressing raw wings before flour dredging.  What a difference! These turned out to be the best wings I've made yet! I've always deep fried them before and I loved the ease of baking. Also placed the floured wings on cooling racks  over aluminum covered baking sheets to bake, turning once during bake time. 25 minutes each side.  I made 2 sauces, dipping half in one and half in the other, and put them under a moderate broiler for 5 minutes to crisp (after baking)  Serve extra sauce on the side--mmm mmm! These were worth the effort---clean up was nothing more than tossing 2 sheets of aluminum foil (and all those lil' bones)  in the trash! Thanks for great suggestions people ~sure made my day!--- PS. I watched chef John's video on  deboning that part of the wing with the double bones--just before you eat it--EASY!! And you didn't miss a single morsel of the meat!! 
Boy have I learned a lot of cool things about Wings!!!

text:
First time making wings, and I'm so glad I read the reviews and followed these tips.  I made sure the wings were very dry (squeezed in paper towels and even had sit in fridge with no cover for an hour on more paper towels, to be sure).  I used gluten free flour which was undetectable to anyone, along with cayenne, garlic powder and salt -  and also added some onion powder.  Went a little heavy on the cayenne, but it was good.  After coating chicken wings/legs, I placed evenly in two foil throw away pans that I had sprayed with coconut oil.  Sat in the fridge for about 4 hours (because I was out running errands).  Then I kept in those pans, cooked for 25 minutes at 425 degrees with no sauce, on each side.  Then added the sauce (I melted 1/2 pound butter and put a bottle of premade wing sauce) into the pan and whisked.  When I tasted it I thought it was a bit too spicy so I looked in my fridge to see what to add to cool it a little....and I had leftover tomato soup, so I put it in - did the trick, and tasted great!  Covered the chicken, then broiled 5 minutes each side.   Was sure to coat the chicken very well with the sauce.  Tasted fantastic!  Was a big hit at a super bowl party.  Will definitely make this again!

I have been making these wings for ages.  The hubby asks for them several times a month. Other than adding more cayenne I have not changed a thing. text:
These wings were awesome.  I don't know why so many others are complaining about the wings being soggy.  I set them in the fridge for about an hour and then baked them for 30 minutes on one side and then 30 minutes on the other side at 425 degrees.  I melted the butter with the hot sauce (use whatever kind you like) on the stove eye just before taking them out of the oven.  Once out, I put them in a big bowl and poured the hot sauce mixture over them and tossed them in it.  We like our wings wet.  They turned out to be wonderful.  Will definitely be making this recipe in the future.  It will be my go to buffalo wing recipe.

As written, I could see how the wings could get soggy.  Put oven to 450.  DON'T put sauce on until the very end.   Use a cooling rack over aluminum foil.  25 minutes, then turn for another 25. text:
I followed the recipe exactly (except the only hot sauce I had was Tapatio), adding the step of patting the wings dry before flouring them. Also, instead of dipping them in the hot sauce/butter mixture, I dripped on some sauce and rubbed the wing to coat it. I think this had the dual effect of a) making sure there was enough sauce to coat all the wings and b) allowing the wings to get delightfully crisp in the oven. Both my husband and I really liked this recipe and we will definitely make it again!

Baked up with a good crispy crunch (though not as much as fried) on a cast iron griddle pan (with the raised ridges) so they weren't sitting in their own grease/sauce and the wings had good flavor. text:
I would never flour my wings before baking, although baking IS preferred over frying. I simply lightly season my wings with whatever tickles my fancy, throw them on a baking sheet(s) covered with "Release" foil and bake for at least an hour at 425, turning once halfway thru and draining off any grease/liquid. Then I put them in a bowl lined with paper towels to absorb any leftover grease and toss with Frank's hot sauce. EASY PEASY!

Followed the recipe except we cut out the cayenne, no one wanted them that hot...I also added chili powder to the flour mixture. We fridged it for an hour like it said (my wings were frozen) I then placed them in a large lasagna glass baking pan...we brushed on the butter hot sauce mixture (we also added a table spoon of brown sugar to that) after brushing it on I then poured the rest over the wings...I baked mine for an hour & 20 mins being they were frozen at 375f and they turned out PERFECT!! Crispy & almost falling off the bone! So delish! I also made another bag with just BBQ sauce on them & the spicy ones were the biggest hit! We also had Tabasco on the side for anyone who wanted more spice but I think ours were just right! This is definitely going to be the way we do wings from now on!!!

text:
very crispy and delicious. I started by drying the wings really really well, even squeezing them a little. I then threw the wings and flour mix in a big ziploc bag and shook it. I left the wings in there for about 40 minutes, then on a tray lined with foil and sprayed with non-stick cooking spray. Baked them at 400 for 25 mins on each side. Whenever I checked on them, I wiped off juices in the pan with a paper towel on tongs just so they don't get soggy. I then dunked them in buffalo wing sauce and threw them back in the oven for 5 mins on each side. They were a little overdone, so next time I'll only put them in 20 mins on each side.

text:
Awesome recipe! These were my personal changes to the original: This is for 12 wing pieces (no tips). I used only two tablespoons of flour, added pinch of salt, 1/4 teaspoon garlic powder, 1/4 teaspoon cayenne pepper, and some fresh ground black pepper. Dry the wings in paper towels then shake in the flour mix; really shake off any extra flour, the wings should be ever so lightly covered. I place the wings on a wire rack (sprayed  with  Pam) then place rack on foil covered sheet pan. Place in fridge (uncovered) for one hour. Bake in preheated oven (400) for 20-30 mins. Flip wings and return to oven for another 20-30 min. I take the wings out and turn the oven to broil ... put the wings under broiler to brown and crisp. If you want crispy wings, do not coat with wing sauce until ready to serve.
Sauce: 1/3-1/2 cup Franks Red Hot sauce, one tablespoon butter, 1/8 teaspoon cayenne pepper, pinch of sugar; warmed in saucepan.

Very good recipe. Like others recommend, be sure to rinse then dry chicken wings before dredging in flour.  Also, I don't dip the wings before baking. I dredge, refrigerate, spray with cooking spray or olive oil misto, bake for about 40 minutes, then toss the crispy baked wings in sauce and serve. The flour makes the skin extra crispy and picks up more of the sauce.

text:
These turned out GREAT!!  I have never made wings before.  I made some modifications.  I dried the wings, put them in flour only, put them in the freezer for 30-40 min to save time.  Put them in the oven with the flour only on a 'speed bake' for 20min, turned them, brushed sauce on them, baked for another 20min, turned them again and brushed more sauce on them to bake for 5 more min, took them out of the oven to then turn them one more time and brush sauce on them one last time.  They had a caramelized and crispy taste.  They were amazing!!  I used a sauce on them that several people referred my husband to try.  It was great!  We will be having these again in the very near future!!

Love this recipe. For sure stuck with the recommendations of 1) making sure the chicken isn't wet 2) applying hot sauce/butter mixture twice (before and half way through baking and 3)baking for longer than 45 min...more like an hour, 4) putting more pepper, garlic and hot sauce and 5) on a slightly higher temp like 400 degrees to get crispy. 

I don't know if you are supposed to or not, but I for sure get as much of the skin off as possible and it still is plenty juicy. 

Enjoy.

text:
These were wonderful!  I was in a rush, and was unable to refrigerate for an hour.  I seasoned the wings with salt and pepper, then put them into the flour mixture.  I baked them for about 30 minutes in a 400 degree oven to crisp them a bit.  Then I started to baste the sauce on them and bake for another 20 minutes.  Finally broiled for another 30 minutes, and turned every 5-10 minutes, basting until the sauce was gone.  Long process but worth the great results!

text:
These wings are all they promise.
I made 1 mistake in preparing these and that was not using a baking sheet with sides. I used a flat sheet and had oil all over my oven but it was worth the mess because the wings were perfect.
I dipped the floured, refrigerated wings in a mixture of oil and butter rather than all butter and didn't add any sauce to the oil before dipping them. After the wings were baked, I dumped them in a bowl with hot sauce and butter. I was a little concerned because I used WP 5000 instead of all-purpose flour because I'm on a low carb diet, but the wings were nonethelss perfect, crisp wings.

text:
better than fried for sure! This is how I did: 1. cut 6-7 wings : 12-14 small wings in total 2. wash and sprinkle 1-2T of essense on the wings 3. arrange them on a rack and refrigerate for an hour or longer 4. preheat the oven at 424'F and bake for 45 min (after first 30 min, turn them over)  5. 1/4C hot wing sauce + 1T butter+2 cloves of crushed garlics; heat it throughly on the stove 6. after wings are baked, coat them with the warm sause 7. enjoy with baked fries (bake'em at the same time)

text:
Per the recommendation of previous reviews, I cooked them on a rack.  I ended making my buffalo sauce a little different.  A little bit of this, a little of that (margarine, paprika, chili powder, onion powder, garlic powder, cayenne, vinegar, habanero sauce, a hint of sugar, ketchup, and BBQ sauce.  I cooked half of the batch with sauce, and half without.  The  ones without sauce came out slightly crispier, but the ones with sauce came out more flavorful, especially since I basted them with 15 min of cooking time left.  Next time I might marinate the chicken with sauce then bread it.  Overall, a great recipe with flexibility and an awesome substitute for the original fried buffalo wings.

text:
I usually fry my buffalo wings before baking it, which is so time consuming so I was eager to try this recipe.  I pretty much followed the recipe (with 1/2 tsp cayenne pepper); I figured the recipe didn't require "20 whole wings", but rather "10 mini-drumsticks & 10 safety pins", which is what we call it in our house.) As suggested, I used a rack to keep the wings crispy.  After turning over, I "basted" it by spooning the drippings.  I also made a dipping sauce using 1/3 c melter butter and 1/3 c hot pepper sauce.  My hubby is a buffalo wing lover, and he gave this recipe the "thumbs up"!

text:
I had never made wings before and these turned out pretty well. I halved the recipe but still put in the 1/2 tsp of cayenne (like the correction review stated) and a 1/4 cup hot sauce (I used Texas Pete because that's all we had). I definitely will make these again but I'll make the following changes: 1) I'll probably double or triple the amount of cayenne and add some additional hot sauce as well. Definitely needed more kick. 2) I'll try cooking it on a rack next time because it ended up swimming the the grease a lot. 3) I will spray the aluminum or rack extremely well with cooking spray because I had some issues with sticking. Otherwise, they weren't soggy at all because I patted and squeezed with a paper towel after rinsing, as well as leaving them in the fridge for about and hour and half.

My first review! I could not stay quiet after eating these! I am a Wing LOVER, and these are the best. CRISPY!! Not saucy!! My wife and I could not stop eating them! Other comments; I had never cooked wings myself, so I did not know that twenty wings, once cut apart, equaled 40 wings. That was OK, we just had more...thank God!
